The most accurate contact angle prediction method was the Panayiotou method, with one contact
angle experimental data from one non-polar liquid. In contrast, it was evident that using a polar
liquid to estimate contact angles with the Panayiotou method leads to erroneous results. On the
other hand, the remaining methods predicted the contact angles for most of the liquids on the
polymer’s surface with reasonable accuracy. In addition, lower deviations were observed when
the examined polymer was non-polar and when the polymer was extensively investigated in the
literature. Table 128 shows the average deviations between the experimental and predicted contact
angles calculated with the four methods. For half of the polymers, the Panayiotou method showed
the lowest average divergences among the approaches. For most cases, the average deviation of the
Panayiotou method was increased due to one experimental data from contact angles. For example,
for PP, the average deviation was increased because of the high divergences between the literature
and the estimated contact angle of DMSO. If DMSO was excluded for PMMA with the Panayiotou
method, the average deviation would equal 4.3%. Thus, one data that remarkably diverges from
96
==PAGE:108==
the experimental may significantly affect the overall average value. Finally, regarding Nylon-6, the
Panayiotou method could not compete with van Oss/Good and Hansen/Beerbower. The assumption
made in the surface tension component calculation in Chapter 7.1.2 seems to affect the accuracy of
the result.
10
Conclusion and Future work
The recently developed innovative method of Panayiotou was used for the surface tension calcula-
tion of various polymers. That method combines quantum chemistry and statistical thermodynam-
ics to provide the partial solvation parameters (PSPs), molecular descriptors linked to Hansen solu-
bility parameters (HSPs). PSPs are used to calculate liquid surface tension components, while they
are required for the polymer’s dispersion and hydrogen-bonding components. Many approaches
were tried to investigate the most efficient for the Panayiotou method. The results clearly showed
that the best approach was the first one with the polymer’s dispersion surface tension component
to be calculated from its analogue oligomer. The polarizability term is calculated from an equation
with one unknown parameter with the assistance of one experimental contact angle data from a non-
polar solvent. Finally, the PSP and polarizability interconnection equations are used for calculating
the hydrogen-bonding component.
Owens/Wendt, van Oss/Good, and Hansen/Beerbower methods were used for comparison with
the Panayiotou method. Panayiotou’s method showed better agreement with the van Oss/Good
theory, where only slightly divergences among the two approaches were observed. These two
methods have a common point in using an asymmetric term for hydrogen-bonding interactions.
Hansen/Beerbower’s method, which uses a symmetric term for these interactions, showed the high-
est divergences between the four methods; however, for many polymers, it worked perfectly.
The contact angle prediction showed that the Panayiotou and van Oss/Good methods were the most
efficient. In addition, the Panayiotou method predicted the liquid’s angles with very low deviations
from the literature reported values for most polymers.
However, the Panayiotou method has a significant limitation. That method requires the knowledge
of the partial solvation parameters (PSPs) and the UNIFAC/UNIQUAC parameters. The limited
reported PSPs of polymers hinder the broad applicability of the method with its more efficient ap-
proach. For calculating these parameters, the knowledge of quantum chemistry is fundamental.
In future work, an experienced quantum chemistry person can evaluate the partial solvation pa-
rameters of various polymers. Furthermore, the two non-polar liquids approach seems to provide
satisfactory results. An extension of that investigation is calculating the polymer’s surface tension
with many liquid pairs.

A.4.6
Analog oligomer approach calculations
Nylon-6 calculations:
Nylon-6 is one of the limited polymers that have not at least one of the acidic and basic partial
solvation parameters zero. That means that the term σGhb is not equal to σGb or σGa, and should
be calculated from (3.5). The dispersion and polarizability surface tensions are calculated similarly
with PCL.

ride, and dodecane are 76.00, 36.00, 42.00 o [36]. Similarly with Teflon FEP, two different pairs of
liquids will be investigated to increase the accuracy of the calculated surface tension.
